<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e3472ef3-825b-4aac-bf64-ba0e67b220d4'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText12194666299835210641" style="display:none">Sabine isn't like anyone else. For as long as she can remember, she's had two lives. Every twenty-four hours she "shifts," living each day twice. In one life, Sabine has everything: popular friends, perfect grades, expensive clothes, and the guy everyone wants. In the other, Sabine's family struggles financially, and her friends are considered rebels. But then she meets Ethan. He's gorgeous and challenging, and he makes her feel like she's never felt before.<br /><br />All Sabine really wants is the chance to live only <i>one</i> life. But when this finally becomes possible, is she willing to risk everything - including losing the one person who might actually believe her - to make it happen?</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1634114402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13216120712049307075"><b>4,5 stars rounded up to 5</b><br/><br/>This was a very refreshing and unique read for me. I literally read it in one sitting. I just couldn’t put it down.<br/><br/>It is kind of paranormal, that can be interpreted as the life of a girl in two parallel dimensions.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463498051ra/19125260.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Sabine has two lives. She describes her situation as follows:<br/><br/><i>
  <b>“I am two people. Neither better than the other, no superpowers, no mystical destinies, no two-places-in-one-time mechanism – but two people. Different in ways fundamental, even though at the most </b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText13216120712049307075" style="display:none"><b>4,5 stars rounded up to 5</b><br><br>This was a very refreshing and unique read for me. I literally read it in one sitting. I just couldn’t put it down.<br><br>It is kind of paranormal, that can be interpreted as the life of a girl in two parallel dimensions.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463498051ra/19125260.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sabine has two lives. She describes her situation as follows:<br><br><i>
  <b>“I am two people. Neither better than the other, no superpowers, no mystical destinies, no two-places-in-one-time mechanism – but two people. Different in ways fundamental, even though at the most basic level I look the same. My physical attributes, my memory and my name follow me. For the past eighteen years, everything else, everything , about me is different. Twenty-four hours as the first of me. And in the blink of an eye, twenty-four hours as the second of me. Every day, without fail, it goes on …” </b>
</i><br><br>She says, <i>
  <b>“Every night, I Cinderella myself from one life to the next” ... “my body clock is different from everyone else’s. There is no loophole. Until now, that is.”</b>
</i><br><br>Every day at midnight, she shifts lives. When she shifts from one life to another, there is no time lapse in the other one. It happens in the blink of an eye. She just goes there, and while she is living 24 hours in the other life, not even one second passes here. So, when she shifts back to the other life, it is like no time has passed, no lapse at all. So noone can realize it. <br><br>*********************************************<br><br>She lives one of her lives in Roxbury and the other in Wellesley. In one life, she has a little sister and in the other she has two brothers. Her parents are different, her friends are different. Her homes are different. Her financial situation and future promises are different in two lives.<br><br>Her body, and anything inherent to her body, which is her mind and memories go to the other life through the Shift. But material things such as clothes or jewellery cannot. Only her name is the same in both lives: Sabine. Nothing else.<br><br>Until the age of 18, physical qualites also went through the Shift. Her injuries, her illnesses and even haircut went through the Shift. <br><br>*********************************************<br><br>At the age of 18, a glitch occured. The rules had changed.<br><br>Her arm was broken in one life but it didn’t go through the Shift to the other life and she was surprised to see her arm was not broken in the other life. <br><br>This led her to do some tests to be sure if no physical crossed over any more. Because if it didn’t, she thought there could be a chance to make sure there was only one of her, by killing the other. <br><br>*********************************************<br><br>Sabine wasn’t happy with leading two lives. Think of it like this. You have one boyfriend here in one life. But you have another boyfriend in another life. But your heart is one and the same and it couldn’t normally belong to two people. That is only one of the complications. Everything was so difficult. She had to finish schools twice in each life. It seems that she has lived 18 years but she felt it as if she lived for 18x2=36 years, doing similar things twice with different people. That is why, she wants a normal life and she knows which life she prefers.<br><br>She only needs to test to make sure if it is possible...<br><br>However, as the saying goes, <b>“Life is what happens when you are busy making other plans” </b>and life brings her unexpected choices and opportunities. <br><br>She has to reconsider everything...<br><br>*********************************************<br><br>Her parents in one life, her boyfriend Dex in the other life and most importantly a very special guy called Ethan in one life change all the plans she has made... <br><br>Oh Ethan, my poor beautiful boy Ethan... He will engrave himself in your heart for sure...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463498051i/19125261._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sabine wants at least one person to really know who she is and love her like that...<br><br><i>
  <b>Without thinking, I lifted my arm towards him, my handcupping his face. His eyes widened, but he didn’t move away. ‘Need someone to know me,’ I murmured. Begged. Because we both knew he still hadn’t answered my question. <br>‘Why?’ he asked, his voice breaking. <br>‘Cause no one ever has... Want a chance … to really live,’ I murmured. </b>
</i><br><br>*********************************************<br><br>This book was a roller coaster of emotions. Even a very simple dialogue like the one below, given the circumstances, made a big impact and caused me to burst into bloody tears:<br><i>
  <b><br>I shot a look at the clock. So did he. One minute till midnight. <br>‘What?’ <br>‘Don’t.’ <br>‘Don’t what?’ <br>‘Don’t do it tonight...’</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463498051i/19125262._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The first half of the book is mostly about how Sabine lives and what things have changed at the age of 18. <br><br>The second half deals with her choice and this second half includes romance and deeper emotions.<br><br>*********************************************<br><br>This is a book in which emotions rise gradually with each page you turn. But as I said, you will feel diverse emotions. <br><br>You will be angry, you will get scared, you will get confused, you will feel doubtful, you will be sad, you will be happy, you will shed tears, sad tears, happy tears... <br><br>The book will give you all.<br><br>*********************************************<br><br>Whatever I feared, it happened.<br>Whatever I hoped, it happened...<br><br>Only.. Only, I wished there would be an epilogue, but there wasn’t. So, I would really appreciate a Book 2 or a novella... something... something more... But, that doesn’t mean that the book doesn’t have a good ending. It does have a very good ending (<i>At least for me, it was good. But if you need a HEA with marriage and kids, maybe you will be disappointed as there is none</i>). <br><br>Still, although I loved how it ended, it just wasn’t enough, I needed more... more time with them... <br><br>Therefore, it is 5 points out of 4,5 for me...<br><br>All in all, this is one of these books you must read, it should’t be missed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13216120712049307075" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_939679559" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/939679559" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/939679559?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408331736" href="/book/show/21842237-between-the-lives">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer939679559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6827975918842054948">Thought provoking and compelling, Between the Lives is a story about a girl with two lives. One is seemingly perfect, but the other has him… <br/><br/>At first this novel reminded me quite a bit of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12926807-lucid' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lucid by Adrienne Stoltz and Ron Bass</a> which I loved, but it ended up standing on its own. While Lucid was more about the mystery, this one is more about big choices and love and life. Often throughout this book I would stop and think about what I would do if I had two lives. Imagine the possibilities! Being abl</span>
  <span id="freeText6827975918842054948" style="display:none">Thought provoking and compelling, Between the Lives is a story about a girl with two lives. One is seemingly perfect, but the other has him… <br><br>At first this novel reminded me quite a bit of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12926807-lucid" rel="nofollow noopener">Lucid by Adrienne Stoltz and Ron Bass</a> which I loved, but it ended up standing on its own. While Lucid was more about the mystery, this one is more about big choices and love and life. Often throughout this book I would stop and think about what I would do if I had two lives. Imagine the possibilities! Being able to basically get an extra 24 hours every day to be a different person, yet the same. I just loved this idea, although I could also understand her wanting to give one up, to be able to fully live in one life instead of having to live a lie twice. <br><br>The double life aspect is built with fantastic attention to detail - though it isn't at all difficult to understand like some sci-fi novels can be. It just has many layers to avoid plot holes or endless questions. Like, what happens with injuries and memories and how both worlds work in terms of each other (if she goes to her "other" home, or tries to find people from the other life, for instance). I also loved how different she was in each life. In one, she seems to have it all. A wealthy family, a future at Harvard, tons of friends, popularity, and the perfect relationship - on the outside (I don't get why she stayed with him if he made her so queasy - I know that he's a constant to her but bleh). In the other, she's kind of a delinquent with nothing much going for her in comparison. But then she meets Ethan just when she decides she's done with this life. Sabine is an 18 year old girl, and teenage girl priorities she has. Her outlook on life is superficial and she can be selfish at times. She may not be the most likeable protagonist, but she's certainly realistically constructed. <br><br>While in one life the romance makes you kind of uneasy, in the other, we've got a wonderful love interest: Ethan who is full of charm and larger-than-life questions. I loved how he gave her a reason to stay, but he didn't make it about himself. He made her think of her double-life as a gift instead of a curse. He also comes with baggage of his own that gives the book some emotional depth as well as a sense of realism that you don't always find in YA romance. Other than romance we have family and parental presence which I appreciated, but what I enjoyed most was the sibling relationships in both lives. One is a young sister who's adorable, the other is the older brother with whom she finally forms a bond. With a smaller role but just as well developed, her friend Capri bring a lot of life to the book and quickly became a favourite of mine. <br><br>Romance, family, life, and second chances; Between the Lives is a wonderfully crafted contemporary story with a sci-fi twist. I would recommend it to those who like stories with a meaning. <br><br>--<br><i>A copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388702323i/7905232.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_929968790" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/929968790" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/929968790?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780802737021" href="/book/show/18594392-one-past-midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer929968790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9367267743824382942">3.5 stars<br/><br/>Also reviewed for <a href='http://www.addicted2heroines.com/2014/07/early-review-one-past-midnight-by.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Addicted2Heroines</a> <br/> <br/>Really interesting idea you have here, right? One girl. Two lives.<br/>Verrry cool.<br/>I think I would have rated it higher If I hadn't seen the ending coming from a mile away. Not that it's a bad ending! Far from it, but I just...knew it would happen. Exactly like it happened.<br/>So I'm thinking that maybe I've just read too many books? Is that possible?<br/><i>Nonsense! Sacrilege!</i><br/>Hear me out before you burn me at the stake, though. I mean, we've pretty much determined </span>
  <span id="freeText9367267743824382942" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />Also reviewed for <a href="http://www.addicted2heroines.com/2014/07/early-review-one-past-midnight-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Addicted2Heroines</a> <br /> <br />Really interesting idea you have here, right? One girl. Two lives.<br />Verrry cool.<br />I think I would have rated it higher If I hadn't seen the ending coming from a mile away. Not that it's a bad ending! Far from it, but I just...knew it would happen. Exactly like it happened.<br />So I'm thinking that maybe I've just read too many books? Is that possible?<br /><i>Nonsense! Sacrilege!</i><br />Hear me out before you burn me at the stake, though. I mean, we've pretty much determined that I'm not smarter than the average bear, so it's not like I puzzled it out with my Sherlock-like deduction skills. The only possible explanation is that I've seen this plot in action before.<br />So. The 'shocker' would work out well for any readers who are younger, haven't read a million books, or frequently have the wool pulled over their eyes while reading stuff. Otherwise, go into this knowing that you'll probably not get a <i>GASP!</i> moment out of it, and you'll be fine.<br /><br />I also felt a little let down by the lack of explanation for Sabine's condition. I know that not everything has a nice and tidy answer, but I was hoping for <i>something</i>. Even an educated guess would have made me happy.<br />Alas, no. The reason she lives two lives is because...she lives two lives.<br /><br />The story revolves around Sabine, and whether or not she can (or should) pick one life to live. Which basically boils down to whether or not she should kill herself. The whole broken arm thing (see the blurb) leads her to believe that she can end it in one life, and still live happily ever after in the other.<br /><i>Ooooooh. Tricky.</i><br />See, in both lives she has some reason to want to stay, but it's unbearably hard for her to keep switching back and forth. And for this reason alone, you kinda want her to be able kill herself in one life. Which was weird, 'cause I don't actually think suicide is a good idea. But at the same time, that whole switching back and forth thing sounded awful.<br />Don't worry, though, the author doesn't seem to condone killing yourself either. Which is nice, considering this is a young adult title.<br />Ok. So if she<i> can</i> make it so she only has one life, then the question naturally turns into <i>which</i> life she should choose.<br />At first it seems pretty easy. Go with the life where your folks haven't stuffed you into a psyche ward, right? <br /><i>Ehhhh. </i><br />Naturally, she meets and falls in love with Mr. Wonderful while she's stuck in the loony bin. And, of course, Mr. Wonderful is the only person who actually <i>believes</i> her about the whole Two-Life thing. But Mr. Wonderful has a <i>SECRET</i>! He repeatedly tells Sabine he doesn't want her to chose not to kill herself because of <i>him</i>, even though it's obvious they have feelings for each other.<br /><i>I'm pretty sure you'll figure out the SECRET if I give you any more information about the book, so I'm just going to shut up now...</i><br />Anyhoo, he wants her to choose to keep both lives because it's a special opportunity. <br /><br />I have to say, I was satisfied with the ending, even though I saw it coming. Also, this is a stand-alone novel, which made it quite a breath of fresh air for me. It was nice to be able to close a book and just be finished with it. <br />All in all, not a bad way to pass the time.<br /><br /><i>Digital arc from NetGalley and the publisher.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9367267743824382942" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=i-cried">i-cried</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=not-bad-at-all">not-bad-at-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=2013-favourites">2013-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=aussie">aussie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=swoony-guys">swoony-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer563300743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13254904793199111446">See more reviews at <a href='http://theyabooklover.blogspot.com.au/' rel='nofollow noopener'>YA Midnight Reads</a><br/><br/><b> Thank you HarperCollins Australia for sending me this copy. No compensation was given or taken to alter this review. </b> <br/><br/><i>'"I want to know that if I drift off to sleep by accident one day, I'll wake up in the same place. I want to live each day once, the best that I can live it. </i> <br/><br/>A powerful book about love or life, Jessica Shirvington introduces readers once again to an intriguing and heart breaking world. While I felt there were somethings I wanted more depth i</span>
  <span id="freeText13254904793199111446" style="display:none">See more reviews at <a href="http://theyabooklover.blogspot.com.au/" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Midnight Reads</a><br /><br /><b> Thank you HarperCollins Australia for sending me this copy. No compensation was given or taken to alter this review. </b> <br /><br /><i>'"I want to know that if I drift off to sleep by accident one day, I'll wake up in the same place. I want to live each day once, the best that I can live it. </i> <br /><br />A powerful book about love or life, Jessica Shirvington introduces readers once again to an intriguing and heart breaking world. While I felt there were somethings I wanted more depth in and for the characters to be more likeable, Between The Lives was a great success that was extremely addictive. One word to describe this book would be; beautiful. <br /><br />Sabine lives two worlds. In one life (Wellesley) she is rich, has a perfect boyfriend and respected; in the other(Roxbury), she is low on money and her life is rather glum. She lives each day twice, once in each of her words, shifting back at 12:00 am every 24 hours. But when Sabine realises that there has been a glitch, her secret becomes exposed and Sabine must choose between life or death, perfect love or life. Sometimes, the smallest things matter greatly.<br /><br />The characters, on majority were rather loveable and relatable. The only flaw I with Sabine was that she never seemed to shut up. She constantly talked for an entire page and I just felt overloaded and confused as she was the main source of info dumping. Other than that, Sabine was pretty close to perfect for someone who managed to change her personality and image in her completely opposite lives. She was sensitive but it was honest and comprehendible in Sabine's circumstances. <br /><br />Ethan was my absolute favourite character. Not only was he creepishly dark and interesting to read about, but also he was easy to relate and admire. He was smart about the way he accomplished things and wasn't naive, but not irritating for being too stubbornly obstinate simultaneously. Jess created such a fascinating supporting character that I simply just fell in love with. One tiny complaint could only be that his way of sharing emotions was rather poor but in the end, and I repeat, in the end, Jess assures us that we will have some sort of satisfaction in one form of another. <br /><br />I was completely blown away with the romance, it was heart-wrenchingly exquisite. Sabine and Ethan are one of the best literary couples I've come across in some time (meaning 3 months) and I simply relished those ravishing scenes. It not only broke my heart, but also opened my eyes that not everything will always go as planned, but in somehow,there is always light in every dark situation. *dies of feels* <br /><br /><i> '"I'm ready, Ethan. You were right. I WAS lost. But you found me, between the lives."'</i> This quote would have to be my star. It is just another example of how beautiful this book is and the prose- oh the prose is magnificent. I cannot press how much the writing skills Jess showed off impacted me. I seriously cannot get over it. <br /><br />Two major flaws: <br />1) The plot. I enjoyed about, 75% of the plot. Jess caught me into this skilfully crafted world gorgeously but what I thought afterwards, in my own smarminess of a summary. A girl who lives in two worlds and tries to kill herself with these unnecessary experiments. In brief, that is pretty much what happened, but Jess <i> just</i> managed to steer slightly away from that problem.<br />2) The unanswered questions. I am constantly annoyed when I am left with unanswered questions from books. What I really wanted to I so was <i>Why does only Sabine have two lives?How did it happen?</i> Quite frankly, this was not answered properly. <br /><br />All in all, Between The Lives was an earth shattering book that really threw my emotions onto the line. I adore Jess' work and will be eager to see more books like these getting written. A story about perfect love or life, this explores hidden emotions and really makes readers think. I recommend to staplers of Jess' The Violet Eden Chapters' as this will cure the thirst and other books with alternate worlds because this, was just as good as any of them. Of course, if you were not a fan of Jess' previous novels, I can still assure you that this may change your decision with large velocity. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13254904793199111446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5126513875340303952" style="display:none">Sometimes, just sometimes, I randomly pick a book off the shelf at the library.       <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer941867817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2066268187632673777"><a href='http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402459641i/9940643.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>3.5 stars<br/><br/>Since this one was my first Jessica Shirvington novel, I really didn't know what to expect from this one. I was hoping for some intriguing, attention-grabbing mystery that would make me question the world and how it works... <em>One Past Midnight</em> gave me exactly what I wanted.<br/><br/>Sabine lived two lives. I was expecting to be a little confused, or maybe bored with at least one of her lives, but Shirvington definitely knows how to keep things exciting. <strong>Every little detail, ever scene from eit</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText2066268187632673777" style="display:none"><a href="http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402459641i/9940643.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>3.5 stars<br><br>Since this one was my first Jessica Shirvington novel, I really didn't know what to expect from this one. I was hoping for some intriguing, attention-grabbing mystery that would make me question the world and how it works... <em>One Past Midnight</em> gave me exactly what I wanted.<br><br>Sabine lived two lives. I was expecting to be a little confused, or maybe bored with at least one of her lives, but Shirvington definitely knows how to keep things exciting. <strong>Every little detail, ever scene from either of Sabine's lives kept me hooked</strong>. Okay, I'll admit--I do have a "favorite" from her two lives, or one that I preferred to read about more, but I really wanted to know more about both of Sabine's lives. <strong>One of them did have a bit more action and happenings, but it was good to take a break from those with the calmness and normality of her other life</strong>. There was really a good balance here, I'd say.<br><br>Now,<strong> Sabine's definitely no perfect character</strong>. In fact, she made a lot of really stupid choices and decisions throughout the novel. Really, I wanted to shake some sense into this girl some time in the middle of the book. The thing is,<strong> I totally saw her growth by the end of the novel</strong>. She finally learned to accept things and to be content with how her life (well, lives) is going to work out.<br><br><blockquote>
  “Life’s too short. If Ethan taught me anything, that would be it. I want to get on with living mine.” 
</blockquote><br><br>I didn't think this one would have romance in it, but it did. <strong>And boy, was Ethan a sweet guy</strong>. Well, at first, I was kind of indifferent to him and wanted him to just walk out and leave, but once <strong>I got to know more about him, the more I wanted him to be part of Sabine's life</strong> (and mine). He was the only person who believed in Sabine, even more than her own parents did.<br><br>The main idea of the book was just so intriguing. I needed to know about why Sabine was the way she was. I needed to know why suddenly things were changing.<strong> If these are also the questions in your head, you'll be disappointed</strong>. These weren't explained in the book at all. You could call this an "air of mystery" or a lack of information. Maybe some things were meant to be left alone and not dwell on any further.<br><br>This "air of mystery" did give way to some unexpected twists. Like I said, I think the book had two major twists. <strong>One was pretty much expected for me</strong>--hints were dropped everywhere, so I wasn't all that shocked. But the book's ending? <strong>Shit, I did not see that coming</strong>. I thought my eyeballs were going to bulge out of my eyes when a certain something happened... Let's just say the ending left me really satisfied, and leave it at that.<br><br>Pacing was perfect during the beginning and the end of the novel. There were a few rushed scenes toward the middle, but most of the time,<strong> my reading experience was pretty smooth</strong> with this one. <strong>Shirvington also had this easy-to-get-into writing style</strong> that made the entire reading process so much easier to go through. I was flipping pages like a pro.<br><br>In conclusion,<em> One Past Midnight</em> will poke at your brain and will make you question how the universe really works. You'll stay up past midnight since you'll want to know how everything wraps up. And trust me, you'll really want to know how this ends.</span>

<div id="review_602518511" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/602518511" />
    <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence"><img alt="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559561558p2/6186603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/602518511?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence">Jeann (Happy Indulgence) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer602518511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15378160188782579668">This review has been posted on <a href='http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2013/07/04/between-the-lives-by-jessica-shirvington-review-two-lives-too-much/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Happy Indulgence.</a> Check it out for more reviews!<br/><br/><b>Actual rating: 4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>As soon as Between the Lives turned up on my doorstep, I started reading it straight away. With such a unique and interesting premise, it captivated me from the moment I read the blurb and saw the cover.<br/><br/>Sabine is a teenager who lives two lives, each completely different to the other. In one life, she’s a rebel who has a less than perfect family, one who is poor and never impressed with her. In </span>
  <span id="freeText15378160188782579668" style="display:none">This review has been posted on <a href="http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2013/07/04/between-the-lives-by-jessica-shirvington-review-two-lives-too-much/" rel="nofollow noopener">Happy Indulgence.</a> Check it out for more reviews!<br /><br /><b>Actual rating: 4.5 stars</b><br /><br />As soon as Between the Lives turned up on my doorstep, I started reading it straight away. With such a unique and interesting premise, it captivated me from the moment I read the blurb and saw the cover.<br /><br />Sabine is a teenager who lives two lives, each completely different to the other. In one life, she’s a rebel who has a less than perfect family, one who is poor and never impressed with her. In the other, she lives a dream life as one of the most popular girls in the school who lives in a wealthy family. Every 24 hours at midnight, she shifts between one life to the next, retaining her memories of each life while she is expected to retain a completely different personality.<br /><br />From describing the challenges in her Roxbury life, to her lack of passion with her ‘perfect’ boyfriend in Wellesley, I was captivated. Sabine has been going through this all of her life (or more appropriate, lives) and she’s clearly learnt how to survive by lying and being what people want her to be. As she nears her 18th birthday, never has she felt so lost. With her constant fear of letting something slip about her other identity and undergoing the traumatic shift at midnight, Sabine has never felt so alone.<br /><br />That is, until she discovers a loophole when she breaks her arm and for the first time, it doesn’t carry over to her next life. She begins a series of terrifying experiments to see whether she can finally choose the life she wants to live. And that’s where everything spirals out of control and she meets the only person who will ever believe her – Ethan.<br /><br />I found Between the Lives to be compelling, intelligent, and thrilling. The author describes the fear and uncertainty that Sabine feels with such clarity that it feels like you’re experiencing it along with her. From her perfect Wellesley life to growing closer to Ethan under less than ideal circumstances, Sabine’s life is fascinating. She’s constantly torn between terrifying circumstances, kind of lost between the two.<br /><br />Ethan and Sabine are a couple that I found myself rooting for, hoping that they would get a happy ever after ending. As Sabine considers ending one life so she can live completely in the other – Ethan teaches her the meaning of living life to the fullest and showing her that love can make the impossible happen. The couple’s lives are sweet yet tragic and they somehow bond in a heart wrenching way.<br /><br />With a powerful ending that pulled at the heart strings, Between the Lives packed a punch with it’s compelling story and beautiful characters that will leave you with a lasting impression. My only complaint, and it is a small one, is that we never really get answers about why Sabine lives two lives. I wish there was a sequel to this but alas, that’s not the case.<br /><br />I received a review copy from HarperCollins Australia in exchange for an honest review. Thank you so much for this opportunity, I absolutely loved the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15378160188782579668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_522319868" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/522319868" />
    <a title="Renée" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7704961-ren-e"><img alt="Renée" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440078563p2/7704961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/522319868?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Renée" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Renée" href="/user/show/7704961-ren-e">Renée</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7704961-ren-e?shelf=jessica-shirvington">jessica-shirvington</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7704961-ren-e?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer522319868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10025891499927490748">Wow. Just wow. I finished Between The Lives about a minute ago, and I still have tears in my eyes. But then again, what's a good Shirvington book without the tears?<br/>Once again, Jessica has managed to completely flip the ideas of the world upside down. Who else would have thought of such a deep and creative idea? <br/>Sabine's story is one that is truly unique. There has been no other like it, much like with Jessica's other series. The way she has had to adjust to her world, or should I say worlds, to </span>
  <span id="freeText10025891499927490748" style="display:none">Wow. Just wow. I finished Between The Lives about a minute ago, and I still have tears in my eyes. But then again, what's a good Shirvington book without the tears?<br />Once again, Jessica has managed to completely flip the ideas of the world upside down. Who else would have thought of such a deep and creative idea? <br />Sabine's story is one that is truly unique. There has been no other like it, much like with Jessica's other series. The way she has had to adjust to her world, or should I say worlds, to learn to cope with them both and then to come to terms with that mentally, is something that we read about and think, 'oh yeah, that'd be cool,' when in reality, it takes so much strength and self control and sense of self to be able to survive through all that and come to terms with who you are.<br />Ethan. What is it with all the hot guys being called Ethan these days? <br />Anyway, these characters that Jessica creates, that are broken and are struggling with secrets and stereotypes that are put on them, are so pivotal to the protagonist’s story and how she grows and changes, not only physically, but emotionally.<br />Choices are what we all have to face, and they can be confusing and can make us unsettled and sometimes have an attitude of just wanting to give up. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17204984.Between_the_Lives" title="Between the Lives by Jessica Shirvington" rel="nofollow noopener">Between the Lives</a> addresses these themes and explores them in a very complex way. Family can give a lot of support in these times, but in Sabine's case, she did the best she could with the two lives she had.<br />Again, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4134859.Jessica_Shirvington" title="Jessica Shirvington" rel="nofollow noopener">Jessica Shirvington</a>'s words and ideas have changed my perspective on life, on how I view things, and my ideas about faith and existence. Jessica is such a talented writer and the worlds that she creates are so well written that I can almost believe that they are the same as the one we live in.<br />This fantasy is so original and inventive that it fits into reality like it was always meant to be there.<br />Five out of five stars.... and thanks for the tears and the heartbreaking letters and words! </span>
  <a data-text-id="10025891499927490748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1026156897" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1026156897" />
    <a title="Zoe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18886219-zoe"><img alt="Zoe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376420353p2/18886219.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1026156897?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoe" href="/user/show/18886219-zoe">Zoe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780802737021" href="/book/show/18594392-one-past-midnight">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Zoe by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4281498-dre">Dre</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18886219-zoe?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18886219-zoe?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1026156897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13254450987329865658"><a href='http://www.deadlydarlings.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img alt='' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394009068i/8795917.png' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>
      <pre>3.5 stars</pre>
    </u>
  </b>
</blockquote><b>This was not perfect by any stretch of the imagination, but it was entertaining, and, in the end, I suppose that's what matters.</b> This was the first Jessica Shirvington book I have read, but I will definitely read more of her work if all of her novels are like this.<br/><br/>For as long as she can remember, Sabine has lived two separate lives which she "shifts" between every 24 hours. In one life (Wellesley), she's a straight A student with an acceptance to Harvard with</span>
  <span id="freeText13254450987329865658" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.deadlydarlings.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394009068i/8795917.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>
      <pre>3.5 stars</pre>
    </u>
  </b>
</blockquote><b>This was not perfect by any stretch of the imagination, but it was entertaining, and, in the end, I suppose that's what matters.</b> This was the first Jessica Shirvington book I have read, but I will definitely read more of her work if all of her novels are like this.<br><br>For as long as she can remember, Sabine has lived two separate lives which she "shifts" between every 24 hours. In one life (Wellesley), she's a straight A student with an acceptance to Harvard with a supportive and loving family. In the other (Roxbury), she is a social outcast living in a family stuck in poverty...but she has someone she truly loves. But when a glitch happens and her secret is revealed, she must choose between two very different things: <b>the perfect love or the perfect life.</b><br><br>As a character, Sabine was pretty well-done. She had her flaws, but they only made her feel more real to you. I liked her intelligence and her practicality. Sure, she made some rash hormone-based decisions at times, but she's a teenager, right? Her train of thought was so relatable. You could <i>feel</i> how annoyed she was at having to live two lives, and how much she just wanted to be "normal."<br><br><b>I think my main critique about <u>One Past Midnight</u> was the lack of explanation for the Shifting.</b> The actual process of the Shifting and what it entails was - like I mentioned - quite detailed and well thought-out, but we never really learn <i>why</i> Sabine Shifts. How is it scientifically possible for her to do this? Why is she the only person who is able to Shift? The lack of answers slightly annoyed me, but I'll admit, not as much as it typically would have because I was simply really entertained throughout. <br><br>Despite some lack of explanation, this is a fantastic novel by Jessica Shirvington and I was quite impressed. Quite entertaining and well-paced, this is a wonderful, and in the end heart-breaking, story about choosing between being with the one you love or having a perfect life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13254450987329865658" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Allyce Cameron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14786420-allyce-cameron"><img alt="Allyce Cameron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402314705p2/14786420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a title="Allyce Cameron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allyce Cameron" href="/user/show/14786420-allyce-cameron">Allyce Cameron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621474729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16956407224547138201">Wow! What a great read! At the beginning Sabine annoyed me and I found it a little hard to relate but as it progressed I found that I just couldn't stop and had to know which life she would choose. And the ending! I think it definitely pushed it over the line for me from being good to something that I would recommend to others. Well done!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2273710512?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K." class="user" itemprop="url" name="K." href="/user/show/5663034-k">K.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=audience-young-adult">audience-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=loveozya">loveozya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=library">library</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=setting-usa">setting-usa</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2273710512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5716196445071851470">Trigger warnings: self harm, vomit, mental health, assault, cancer, death of a loved one. <br/><br/>I have literally had like a dozen students tell me to read this over the past two years. So when no one had borrowed it over the summer break, I figured I'd finally read it. Aaaaaaaaaaaand NOPE. Like, THE BIGGEST NOPE TO EVER NOPE. <br/><br/>I'm just going to go ahead and bullet point my thoughts because it's easier. <br/><br/>- This is kind of like Every Day by David Levithan, except that 18 year old Sabine just jumps between</span>
  <span id="freeText5716196445071851470" style="display:none">Trigger warnings: self harm, vomit, mental health, assault, cancer, death of a loved one. <br /><br />I have literally had like a dozen students tell me to read this over the past two years. So when no one had borrowed it over the summer break, I figured I'd finally read it. Aaaaaaaaaaaand NOPE. Like, THE BIGGEST NOPE TO EVER NOPE. <br /><br />I'm just going to go ahead and bullet point my thoughts because it's easier. <br /><br />- This is kind of like Every Day by David Levithan, except that 18 year old Sabine just jumps between two bodies.<br />- One is rich, one is poor. In the rich one, she doesn't like her siblings or her boyfriend, but she's rich, so... In the poor one, her little sister is the actual best but she hates literally everything else about her life.<br />- When she breaks her arm as Poor!Sabine and realises it doesn't transfer to Rich!Sabine, she decides this means she can finally CHOOSE BETWEEN HER LIVES.<br />- She goes about this by cutting herself multiple times to test whether her injuries will transfer to Rich!Sabine, then she plans on taking pills to REALLY test the theory<br />- But her parents bust her and send her to a psychiatric facility<br />- At the psychiatric facility, she a) takes a bunch of drugs to see if she can die, and b) meets a guy named Ethan<br />- Ethan is her psychiatric nurse. He's a fully qualified nurse and also doing a post-grad qualification in psychiatry. So, like, he's CLEARLY in at least his mid-20s. Once again, she's EIGHTEEN.<br />- He's also HER PSYCHIATRIC NURSE AND SHOULD NEVER BE HER FUCKING LOVE INTEREST BECAUSE HE'S IN A POSITION OF POWER OVER HER<br />- The whole thing takes place over the course of about two weeks, and he tells her he loves her before they've even kissed<br />- Rich!Sabine's boyfriend beats the shit out of her when she decides she's not ready to sleep with him<br />- Ethan turns out to be at the psychiatric hospital because HE'S DYING OF CANCER BUT DOESN'T WANT TO GIVE UP HIS JOB???? <br />- She finds this out when he literally dies, inexplicably leaving her his apartment, car, and money in his will<br />- Meanwhile in Rich!Sabine's life, Ethan turns out to be one of her brother's friends only it's a different Ethan because he's alive but it's the same Ethan because he looks exactly the same and has this weird sense that he knows her??? <br /><br />Basically, this was problematic thing after problematic thing. I hated the romance side of the story. I basically wanted to set this on fire from start to finish. And I'm going to be deleting it from the system when I start back at work because romantic relationships between teenage girls and their PSYCHIATRIC NURSES SHOULD NOT EXIST BECAUSE THAT IS RAPE JFC. Okay I'm done ranting now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5716196445071851470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_959844167" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/959844167" />
    <a title="Dre" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4281498-dre"><img alt="Dre" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376965889p2/4281498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/959844167?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dre" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dre" href="/user/show/4281498-dre">Dre</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408331736" href="/book/show/21842237-between-the-lives">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4281498-dre?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4281498-dre?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4281498-dre?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4281498-dre?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4281498-dre?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer959844167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2570311136020208373">It was a slow start, but it picked up after Ethan showed up. I was expecting an explanation about this two lives aspect. I wanted more. I expected the ending, but I was anticipating a different one. (Full review to come)<br/><br/><blockquote>The perfect life or the perfect love. You choose.</blockquote><br/><strong>Between The Lives</strong> or <em>One Past Midnight</em> is my first Jessica Shirvington novel, so I was quite excited to dive into the story. Based on the tagline of the book, I was instantly intrigued. Who wouldn't be interested to find out how th</span>
  <span id="freeText2570311136020208373" style="display:none">It was a slow start, but it picked up after Ethan showed up. I was expecting an explanation about this two lives aspect. I wanted more. I expected the ending, but I was anticipating a different one. (Full review to come)<br /><br /><blockquote>The perfect life or the perfect love. You choose.</blockquote><br /><strong>Between The Lives</strong> or <em>One Past Midnight</em> is my first Jessica Shirvington novel, so I was quite excited to dive into the story. Based on the tagline of the book, I was instantly intrigued. Who wouldn't be interested to find out how the two lives work? <strong>It's not pretending to be another person, but you're literally being thrown to another life at midnight. </strong><br /><br />We follow the mundane life of Sabine. Coincidentally, her name is the same in both lives. Every day at midnight, she <em>shifts</em> into her other life. For 17 years, she has lived it every day, knowing full well that material things don't cross over, but whatever physical changes she has, do.<strong> When she turned 18, something strange happened. Sabine feels different.</strong><br /><br />In Roxbury, she lives with hardworking parents, and a sister, Maddie. She loves Maddie to bits, but she doesn't have a perfect relationship with her parents, specially with her father. Her parents manage a drugstore, but they are struggling with money. In this life, she's not the perfect daughter. <strong>She is a sort of delinquent, with nothing much going for her.</strong><br /><br />In Wellesley, her life is somewhat perfect. She has two brothers, Lucas and Ryan, her parents are divorced, but her mother dotes on her. They are wealthy, and she's quite popular in school. She is in a relationship with Dex, one of the cool boys in her high school. Her future consists of Harvard, and she's looking forward to graduating soon.<br /><br />Sabine wants to choose between her two lives, so she conducts experiments to find out if she could leave the other life, and permanently live just the one life she chooses. There was a part in her experiment that made me cringe! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She was self-harming, and was hacking her thigh with dull scissors. Did it make you cringe, too? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> With that in mind, I kept thinking, <i>is she the only one living two lives? Is she living in the same timeline as her other life? Is she a scientific experiment? Do her parents, who manage a drugstore, know about her shifting? </i><br /><br />To be honest, it was a slow start for me. I couldn't fully grasp the book until I reached 20%. I think it was about the same time the character, Ethan, came into the picture in her Roxbury life.<br /><blockquote>That deep, ocean blue eyes.</blockquote><br />Let's talk about Ethan. He's such a sweet guy, but he annoyed me at first. He had the I-don't-care-about-anyone-but-myself attitude when they first met. I think that he is a good influence on Sabine. She was basically planning on ending her life from one of her lives so that she can <em>actually live.</em> But with Ethan in the picture, it made it harder for her to choose.<br /><br />Ethan taught her the meaning of life, and that she needs to think things through before she does something drastic. I was actually rooting for them, because Sabine's relationship with Dex in Wellesley is not as perfect as it seems. And clearly, Sabine doesn't really want to be with him. (She counts every second of their kiss, which she couldn't stand.) So anyway, I had this feeling that Ethan was hiding a secret, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(and I wanted the secret to be that he also shifts, but it was something else.)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and I was a bit wary of his character, but at the same time, I liked how it wasn't instant love between the two. There was a build-up in the romance, and I really loved that they didn't like each other right off the bat.<br /><br />It was really hard for Sabine to live two lives without having anyone to talk to about it. What she wanted was someone to believe her, that she's not crazy. And she found it in Ethan.<br /><blockquote>You said you wanted someone to know you. Maybe I just want to have someone to know me too. Without you in this world, the memories of every moment we've shared together will be gone. We only exist because others see us. Part of my existence...' he swallowed, '...an important part, only exists because you are here to see it.</blockquote><br />There were so many convenient coincidences, too, specially during the time when Ethan was testing Sabine. Like, <em>hmm, I need to translate this Finnish phrase. Oi, the receptionist is Finnish! </em>And I also encountered an inconsistency, which I let slide. There were twists in the book that kind of surprised me, but the major freaking twist was the ending.<br /><br /><strong>I found the ending bordering on cheesy.</strong> I kind of predicted it, but I was hoping that I was wrong. Now, I'm not saying that it was a bad ending, but it basically made me ask more questions about the plot of the book. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Like, if the same person can exist in both lives,*cough* Ethan *cough*, then there's this whole possibility that Sabine is actually TWO persons! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It seriously wrecked my theory.<br /><br />I was discussing the ending with Aimee of <a href="http://deadlydarlings.wordpress.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Deadly Darlings</a>. I asked her if she was bothered that Sabine's shifting into another life wasn't explained at all, and she said she was a bit bothered, but she let it slide. I really wanted the paranormal or scientific explanation of her shifting. If I had my way, I would have preferred that it ended with Sabine being locked up somewhere with schizophrenia. That would have given me the explanation of shifting during midnight, and living an alternate life. And I'd give this book a 5.<br /><br />Overall, it was a good read. But I really wanted answers. Still, if you take away the paranormal element in the book, I'd say it's something that you'd enjoy reading on a rainy Sunday afternoon. #<br /><br /><em>ARC provided by the publisher via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.</em></span>
  <a data-text-id="2570311136020208373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_927147122" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/927147122" />
    <a title="Tanja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2733854-tanja"><img alt="Tanja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376687513p2/2733854.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/927147122?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanja" href="/user/show/2733854-tanja">Tanja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408331736" href="/book/show/21842237-between-the-lives">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2733854-tanja?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2733854-tanja?shelf=21th-century">21th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2733854-tanja?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2733854-tanja?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer927147122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5679124709337809496">I was sure that I was gonna love this book. After all, it's about a girl (Sabine) who has two lives; she lives one for 24 hours and than she shifts to the other. She's been like that for as long as she can remember. But something has changed now - when she breaks her arm in one life, she thinks it's gonna be broken in her other life too, but then she shifts and her arm is fine. So she thinks she may be able to die in one life and keep living the other. All she has to do is pick a life. <br/><br/>Sabine is</span>
  <span id="freeText5679124709337809496" style="display:none">I was sure that I was gonna love this book. After all, it's about a girl (Sabine) who has two lives; she lives one for 24 hours and than she shifts to the other. She's been like that for as long as she can remember. But something has changed now - when she breaks her arm in one life, she thinks it's gonna be broken in her other life too, but then she shifts and her arm is fine. So she thinks she may be able to die in one life and keep living the other. All she has to do is pick a life. <br /><br />Sabine is 18-years-old but she has lived every day twice, so she has actually lived for 36 years. She's still really immature. When her parents catch her with knives and pills that she used to test her I-can-get-rid-of-one-life theory, they want an explanation. Instead of making something up, she tells them the truth. Of course they think she's crazy so she ends up in a hospital. <br /><br />In one life (Roxbury life) she lives with her parents and her little sister. In her Wellesley life, she lives with her mother and two brothers. In Roxbury she's poor, in Wellesley she's rich. Also, in Wellesley she has a boyfriend Dex. He's described as the perfect boyfriend and he loves her so much, but she doesn't really like him. She's only dating him because... well, I actually don't know why. Maybe because she's fucking dumb? Why the hell would you date somebody you aren't interested in? I felt really sorry for Dex (at first). I hated what he did later on in the book. <br /><br />I don't understand why is her Wellesley life considered the 'perfect life'. Is it just because of the money? Cause I can't really see what else is better. It's definitely not because of the boyfriend. <br /><br />The character I actually liked (at first) was Ethan. He works in the hospital she's in. I liked the tests he gave her. It was pretty much the only way I could think of for her to prove that she has two lives. I get that they liked each other but 'falling in love'? I didn't really buy that. <br /><br />It's difficult to believe that her parents never noticed anything strange when she was a kid. If she really thought that everybody has two lives, she probably mentioned something sometimes. Maybe she would talk about her other family or ask somebody what their other life is like. And why is she so terrified of the Shift? It doesn't make sense. <br /><br />If I was her, I would never want to get rid of either life. Having two lives seems great (maybe confusing sometimes, but still great). I loved the premise of the book and if there are any books similar to this I'd love to read them. But this one just wasn't very good. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5679124709337809496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_954021585" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/954021585" />
    <a title="Shannon (It Starts At Midnight)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8652150-shannon-it-starts-at-midnight"><img alt="Shannon (It Starts At Midnight)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595730753p2/8652150.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/954021585?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon (It Starts At Midnight)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon (It Starts At Midnight)" href="/user/show/8652150-shannon-it-starts-at-midnight">Shannon (It Starts At Midnight)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780802737021" href="/book/show/18594392-one-past-midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer954021585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11505106439960257060">Let’s get it out of the way: I loved this book. It made me smile, it made me cry, it made me laugh, it made me think, it pretty much checked every single emotional box. There were characters I loved, characters I hated, and pretty much every imaginable character in between.<br/><br/>Sabine lives two lives, switching between them every 24 hours. No one else knows that she lives both lives, and she is careful to keep them separate. In one life, she comes from a wealthy family, is popular, and has the seemin</span>
  <span id="freeText11505106439960257060" style="display:none">Let’s get it out of the way: I loved this book. It made me smile, it made me cry, it made me laugh, it made me think, it pretty much checked every single emotional box. There were characters I loved, characters I hated, and pretty much every imaginable character in between.<br /><br />Sabine lives two lives, switching between them every 24 hours. No one else knows that she lives both lives, and she is careful to keep them separate. In one life, she comes from a wealthy family, is popular, and has the seemingly perfect friends and boyfriend. In the other, she comes from the “wrong side” of town, complete with a messy family situation, and only one true friend, but a sister that she adores. But, the lying and switching between lives has taken a huge toll on Sabine’s psyche, and she is eager to find a way out. When she breaks her arm in one life and it (for the first time) doesn’t transfer to the other life, she tries to see just how far she can push things, if maybe she can leave one life behind for good.<br /><br />Of course, things aren’t that easy, and Sabine finds herself in some precarious situations in both lives. Along the way, she meets Ethan, the one person who might actually believe that her lives are real. Ethan is… sigh. We all need an Ethan.<br /><br />I can’t talk much more about any of the characters or plot points without giving stuff away, unfortunately. But my heart broke for Sabine time and time again. How isolating, how confusing, how scary her situation would be. Never knowing who to trust, or which path to choose; always having to keep every detail of a full second life fresh in your mind would be hellish. I could absolutely feel every bit of Sabine’s anguish. She also grew remarkably as a character during the book, which was so wonderful to watch.<br /><br />I raced through reading this, unable to put it down, begging to know what choices Sabine would make, or what the ramifications in one life would be on the other. This is the kind of book that makes you think “what if?” the entire time.<br /><br />The end wasn’t cut and dry, nor did it wrap everything up in a neat little package. But it worked. And it made me feel hopeful, without it feeling unbelievable.<br /><br />This is the first book I’ve read by Jessica Shirvington, but it will definitely not be the last. With well fleshed-out characters, an exciting and thought provoking plot, and lots of emotional connection, One Past Midnight earned itself a spot on my favorites list!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11505106439960257060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781743098110" href="/book/show/17730039-between-the-lives">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10378346-louisa?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10378346-louisa?shelf=2013-read">2013-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10378346-louisa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10378346-louisa?shelf=i-ugly-sobbed">i-ugly-sobbed</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer610045872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1014225365934239822"><b>(Actual rating: 3.5 stars)</b><br/><br/>Those last few chapters COMPLETELY DESTROYED ME. Thanks, Aussie YA authors, for constantly making me have all of the feelings!<br/><br/><i>Between the Lives</i> is an interesting take on the "You only live once" school of thought. We all know that. But Sabine literally cannot #YOLO - because she lives two lives, in two slightly different worlds, in completely different circumstances, wholly under the control of something she refers to as the Shift. At midnight every night, she Shifts to</span>
  <span id="freeText1014225365934239822" style="display:none"><b>(Actual rating: 3.5 stars)</b><br /><br />Those last few chapters COMPLETELY DESTROYED ME. Thanks, Aussie YA authors, for constantly making me have all of the feelings!<br /><br /><i>Between the Lives</i> is an interesting take on the "You only live once" school of thought. We all know that. But Sabine literally cannot #YOLO - because she lives two lives, in two slightly different worlds, in completely different circumstances, wholly under the control of something she refers to as the Shift. At midnight every night, she Shifts to the other Sabine. She can't do anything to her Roxbury self, like dye a hidden section of her hair pink, without it affecting her Wellesley self, causing her to have to delicately balance her two lives in order not to tip anyone off. But when she breaks her arm as her Roxbury self and discovers she remains unharmed in her Wellesley life, she starts experimenting.<br /><br />The reason behind the Shift is never explained. That's something I'm more than a little peeved about, as well as the lengths Sabine took in her 'experiments', given that she's intelligent beyond her years (literally). I don't want to talk about the book without giving much away, but those last few chapters? Yeah, redeemed whatever happened before. There are a number of things I could point out that annoyed me, especially how Sabine tries to kill herself multiple times, but at the end of the day this is a compelling, emotional story that I would definitely recommend, if just for Ethan.<br /><br />Brb crying some more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1014225365934239822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
