<div id="review_599390832" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/599390832" />
    <a title="Summer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14778159-summer"><img alt="Summer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574406694p2/14778159.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/599390832?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Summer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Summer" href="/user/show/14778159-summer">Summer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780802737021" href="/book/show/18594392-one-past-midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14778159-summer?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14778159-summer?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14778159-summer?shelf=2014-favorites">2014-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14778159-summer?shelf=scifi-thriller">scifi-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer599390832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11761701490433826932"><i>Thank you Bloomsbury for sending me this copy, which did not affect my review in any way.</i><br/><br/>Beware of slightly unintelligible gushing and if you hear a fangirl sobbing in the distance, that's probably me.<br/><br/>Sabine is a high school senior in her last weeks of school. She lives two lives; one that is seemingly flawless, while the other is - flawed, to say the least. After an unfortunate butt-in-the-air accident, Sabine finds that her physical body is only affected in one life, and not in the other. She </span>
  <span id="freeText11761701490433826932" style="display:none"><i>Thank you Bloomsbury for sending me this copy, which did not affect my review in any way.</i><br /><br />Beware of slightly unintelligible gushing and if you hear a fangirl sobbing in the distance, that's probably me.<br /><br />Sabine is a high school senior in her last weeks of school. She lives two lives; one that is seemingly flawless, while the other is - flawed, to say the least. After an unfortunate butt-in-the-air accident, Sabine finds that her physical body is only affected in one life, and not in the other. She decides that she must choose one life - which is far easier said than done. <br /><br />I like to think of <i>One Past Midnight</i> as the child of <i>Before I Fall</i> by Lauren Oliver and <i>Just Like Fate</i> by Cat Patrick and Suzanne Young. That is, if all the good genes of <i>Before I Fall</i> were dominant and all the bad genes of <i>Just Like Fate</i> were recessive. (There was far too much nerdiness in that sentence to be acceptable.) (My goal exactly.)<br /><br />Basically, if you were to combine the plots of <i>Before I Fall</i> and <i>Just Like Fate</i>, you'd get this beauty of a novel. Which is unique in its own right, I must add.<br /><br />At the start, Sabine, the protagonist, is... unlikable. In both lives. She makes stupid, reckless decisions and can sway to the melodramatic at times throughout the novel. But you know what? She had flaws. She's human. She jumped off the pages and made an impression. And I loved her for that.<br /><br />Should I even be surprised that an Aussie writer has lovely writing? Seriously, it was perfect and Sabine's voice was unforgettable.<br /><br />I loved loved loooved how Shirvington portrayed the sister relationship in one life, and the brother relationship in the other. Family is very important in this novel, and at several points I was half-squealing-half-weeping from their relationships. Kind of like On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta (YUP - I WENT THERE).<br /><br />And call me a sappy teen if you like, but that ending had me balling. Not only that, but Ethan made me "awww!" about a bajillion million times. To tell you the truth, I saw the ending coming from the middle of the book. Did that lessen the amount of tears I cried? HAHAHA NOPE. Beautiful ending is beautiful (and inspiring, and special, and - JUST READ THE BOOK OKAY?)<br /><br />If you're a sensitive emotional wreck like me, then read this. Even if you're the most composed person on the planet, I implore you to read this eye-opening novel. (That is an order.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11761701490433826932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1012107285" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1012107285" />
    <a title="Çavlan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31501360-avlan"><img alt="Çavlan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500021843p2/31501360.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1012107285?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Çavlan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Çavlan" href="/user/show/31501360-avlan">Çavlan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780802737021" href="/book/show/18594392-one-past-midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1012107285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12423553353177083554">If you're interested in parallel worlds and alternate realities, then this one is for you. Great concept, very interesting storyline, compelling characters and the writing is fantastic. Maybe the twist at the end is a little bit predictable but all in all the ending is very satisfying. It might be one of the best YA books I've read this year.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_547066080" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/547066080" />
    <a title="Rashika (is tired)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8492956-rashika-is-tired"><img alt="Rashika (is tired)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476647072p2/8492956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/547066080?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rashika (is tired)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rashika (is tired)" href="/user/show/8492956-rashika-is-tired">Rashika (is tired)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=realistic-contemporary">realistic-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=totally-worth-it">totally-worth-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=cute-love-interests">cute-love-interests</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer547066080" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16418397314286510265"><b> Actual Rating 3.5 </b><br/><br/>After being disappointed by Just like Fate, I decided to pick up Between the Lives which had a similar concept. I was hoping to prove (to myself) that books that are based on this concept didn't all have to turn out bad, and I was right. This book provided me with a very interesting journey, and I was all set to give it a four until the last couple pages.<br/><br/>I am going to start off by saying that while the main character wasn't always likeable, she had a strong voice. Sometimes it</span>
  <span id="freeText16418397314286510265" style="display:none"><b> Actual Rating 3.5 </b><br /><br />After being disappointed by Just like Fate, I decided to pick up Between the Lives which had a similar concept. I was hoping to prove (to myself) that books that are based on this concept didn't all have to turn out bad, and I was right. This book provided me with a very interesting journey, and I was all set to give it a four until the last couple pages.<br /><br />I am going to start off by saying that while the main character wasn't always likeable, she had a strong voice. Sometimes it just bothered me thar she didn't think at all about her other family. She loved them but she kept trying to find an easy way out. I understand why, I do, but that didn't stop me from being frustrated.<br /><br />This story starts with the main character falling down the subway stairs and breaking her wrist. When she 'shifts' to her other life, it turns out that her wrist isn't broken. So are the rules changing? She wants a normal life, which is understandable, and so this was kind of a breakthrough for her, a way out of this whole situation and so she starts experimenting. When her parents find out, she decided to confess, which of course leads them into thinking that she is crazy.<br /><br />Even with how things turned out when she confined in her parents, I was glad she did because it proves that she really wants someone to believe her and to help her.<br /><br />Moving on to her parents. The author did a great job with them. There were two sets of them and each of the sets came with their flaws and their plus points, but more than that the author took some time to develop the parents as well. Her dad from her Roxbury life initially comes across as a bad guy but by the end of the book, I didn't hate him.<br /><br />I really did like the development in her relatinship with her brothers in her Wellesley life. At first I really did not like how the author rolled them out but there was more to them and being the older sibling, I can understand in some ways (I am not justifying their actions here just saying I understand).<br /><br />Her friends, though they didn't play such a significant part, were not actually just flat characters. They seemed to care about her and always asked when they thought something was wrong. One would assume that in her perfect life, her friends would be completely shallow but they weren't, which I was glad for.<br /><br />Now to Ethan… Ethan.. was just..he was definitely one of the better love interests I’ve read about. I’ll admit to initially thinking things were moving too fast between them but I overlooked it because the author did take the time to develop their friendship before she did anything else. <br /><br />My first problem arises with the science aspect behind what was happening to her. I am going to go out on a limb here and compare this book with Every Day. While the latter was strictly a contemporary book, there was still this need in A (the main character) to find out why he/she was the way he/she was. Sabine on the other hand, just wanted a way out and that disappointed me because there wasn’t a lot of exploration into why she was the way she was. As a science geek I really would have liked that.<br /><br />However my main problem with this book was the last couple of pages. Now I cannot say what happened but the event just seemed to come out of nowhere. I didn't think it was necessary. On top of that what happened right at the end was just plain cheesy. It just seemed like the easy way out. The author could have left the book with an open ending and that would have been a whole lot better.<br /><br />On the whole, despite the ending that bothered the hell out of me, I would definitely recommend this. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16418397314286510265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_544280505" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/544280505" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5501124-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581282691p2/5501124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/544280505?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/5501124-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=aussie">aussie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=aussie-ya-read-in-2013">aussie-ya-read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=usa">usa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=i-have-a-copy">i-have-a-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=review-on-the-blog">review-on-the-blog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=female-pov">female-pov</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer544280505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15865275734451542757"><i>Between the Lives</i> by Jessica Shirvington is set in Roxbury and in Wellesley, Massachusetts. I haven’t read any of Jessica’s previous books, but when this was offered for review it sounded too intriguing to turn down. In both lives she’s eighteen years old and named Sabine. In one life she lives in Roxbury, Boston, with her younger sister, Maddie, and her two hard-working parents. In her other life she lives in Wellesley, Massachusetts with her recently divorced mother, and she has two older brot</span>
  <span id="freeText15865275734451542757" style="display:none"><i>Between the Lives</i> by Jessica Shirvington is set in Roxbury and in Wellesley, Massachusetts. I haven’t read any of Jessica’s previous books, but when this was offered for review it sounded too intriguing to turn down. In both lives she’s eighteen years old and named Sabine. In one life she lives in Roxbury, Boston, with her younger sister, Maddie, and her two hard-working parents. In her other life she lives in Wellesley, Massachusetts with her recently divorced mother, and she has two older brothers, Ryan and Lucas.<br /><br />I liked Sabine from the start, she had a strong voice as a narrator and while a lot of people might think it would be fun to have two lives, she’s clearly unhappy and lonely. She can’t discuss it with anyone for fear of them thinking that she’s mentally unstable, so she does her best to remember which life she’s living, and focuses on pleasing her friends and families.<br /><br />Meeting Ethan changes everything for her, he’s the only one who takes an interest in her story and wants to figure out if she’s telling the truth. He seemed like a really good guy, and I was kept guessing as to what was going on with him until the very end.<br /><br />The two lives were handled really well, with plenty of explanation. At midnight Sabine shifts and spends 24 hours in that life. At midnight she shifts back to midnight again and continues on with that day. She doesn't ever miss a day, or even a minute, she lives every day twice but there are differences between each life. I never felt confused, even though I was expecting to with such a topic.<br /><br />I was really surprised by how much I enjoyed this, I was captivated by Sabine’s two lives and keen to see which one she’d choose to keep if she found it to be possible. The ending was sad and a bit of a shock to me, but quite clever, too.<br /><br /><i>Between the Lives</i> is a clever, realistic sci-fi sure to please fans of YA.<br /><br />Thank you to the lovely people at Harper Collins for my review copy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15865275734451542757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1767316045" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1767316045" />
    <a title="Aya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32740224-aya"><img alt="Aya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475251203p2/32740224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1767316045?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aya" href="/user/show/32740224-aya">Aya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1767316045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2896758038390125057">This book's about a girl, named Sabine, who was born twice, in two parallel worlds, juggling between her two lives thinking it was a common thing. Until the day she realises she was actually alone in this. <br/>Not being able to share her newly discovered secret with anyone, fearing to be misjudged, she went on with her lives, "shifting" every 24 hours at midnight and simply accepting the fact that there was nothing she could do about it. But fate decided otherwise. Sabine accidentally broke her arm </span>
  <span id="freeText2896758038390125057" style="display:none">This book's about a girl, named Sabine, who was born twice, in two parallel worlds, juggling between her two lives thinking it was a common thing. Until the day she realises she was actually alone in this. <br />Not being able to share her newly discovered secret with anyone, fearing to be misjudged, she went on with her lives, "shifting" every 24 hours at midnight and simply accepting the fact that there was nothing she could do about it. But fate decided otherwise. Sabine accidentally broke her arm in her Roxbury life, and, thinking the damage would travel with her to her second life in Wellesley, as has always been the case, she started panicking not knowing what excuse to come up with this time, especially since she was to celebrate her birthday in her Wellesley life, and showing up with a broken arm was just not an option.<br />To her great surprise (and confusion), the cast and fracture and pain were gone after the "Shift". Now armed with this new knowledge, she started conducting a series of experiments that might eventually get her to the life she's always dreamed of, one normal life in which she wouldn't have to pretend to be someone she's not.<br />I found the idea very interesting and started this book expecting a pinch of science here and there, exploring the fascinating Multiverse Theory, but to my great disappointment there was no mention of that. Hence the 4 stars.<br />Aside from that, it was a decent read that managed to keep me hooked until the very last page. Wouldn't reaaaaaaally recommend it to any Sci-fi fans, it'll only frustrate your curious longing souls.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2896758038390125057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1634884381" />
    <a title="Bookylicious" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48845552-bookylicious"><img alt="Bookylicious" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460193374p2/48845552.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1634884381?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookylicious" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookylicious" href="/user/show/48845552-bookylicious">Bookylicious</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1634884381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5256262320167350010">This book was what I needed at the moment. I couldn't put it down. Totally a page turner. The writing style was not quite the best I read but it was totally ok for me because the plot was unquestionably unique. However it was toooo short. I needed more. I needed more time with ethan and sabines love. Maybe that was how it should be I don't know. Maybe the writer chose to write this way because of her 2 lives. I couldn't quite feel their love.<br/>Sabine has 2 totally different lifes. She shifts lifes</span>
  <span id="freeText5256262320167350010" style="display:none">This book was what I needed at the moment. I couldn't put it down. Totally a page turner. The writing style was not quite the best I read but it was totally ok for me because the plot was unquestionably unique. However it was toooo short. I needed more. I needed more time with ethan and sabines love. Maybe that was how it should be I don't know. Maybe the writer chose to write this way because of her 2 lives. I couldn't quite feel their love.<br />Sabine has 2 totally different lifes. She shifts lifes at midnight. in one life she is rich, she has a seperated mom and dad, two brothers, friends and a beautiful future ahead. In her alternate life has a younger sister, married mom and dad and also nice friends. In both lifes she has her memory with her. Like if she can talk in french in one life she can also speak fluently in the other life as well..She lived like this until the age of 18. But at the age of 18 she discovers that not pain, injuries or physical differences pass to the other life. when she broke her arm in one life, she was totally healthy in the other one. After she realised this she starts some experiments on herself. But nothing turned out to be what she was expecting....<br />At the end I had lots of questions to the writer. I can't say that nothing major left unanswered. So I need an epilogue or a book #2.<br /></span>

</a><br/><br/><em>"I want to know that if I drift off to sleep by accident one day, I'll wake up in the same place. I want to live each day once, the best that I can live it."</em><br/><br/>What an interesting concept!! This book was unlike anything I've ever read before! I loved the idea of it, and I couldn't put it down. How terrible would it be to fall asleep at night and wake up as someone else the next day, day in and day out?! I can't even imagine!<br/><br/>This book was mostly a contemporary slash romance, with sci-fi elements</span>
  <span id="freeText8593439450562917949" style="display:none"><a href="http://novelheartbeat.com/blog/" rel="nofollow noopener">

I want to live each day once, the best that I can live it."</em><br><br>What an interesting concept!! This book was unlike anything I've ever read before! I loved the idea of it, and I couldn't put it down. How terrible would it be to fall asleep at night and wake up as someone else the next day, day in and day out?! I can't even imagine!<br><br>This book was mostly a contemporary slash romance, with sci-fi elements. It was just the right blend for me, even though I don't usually do romance. But the romance in this was super sweet and endearing! I thought it was awesome that Ethan would ask Sabine questions right before she Shifted to prove that her other world was real!<br><br>THE ENDING!! Oh my lord! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was starting to suspect that something was wrong with Ethan, but oh my goodness I was sobbing! I can't really say much else without spoiling things, but I highly recommend this one. It's such a beautiful story!<br><br><br><b>This review was originally posted on Novel Heartbeat. <div id="review_1223838393" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1223838393" />
    <a title="Dark Faerie Tales" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2766672-dark-faerie-tales"><img alt="Dark Faerie Tales" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1253675501p2/2766672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1223838393?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dark Faerie Tales" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dark Faerie Tales" href="/user/show/2766672-dark-faerie-tales">Dark Faerie Tales</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780802737021" href="/book/show/18594392-one-past-midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2766672-dark-faerie-tales?shelf=reviewed-by-bridget">reviewed-by-bridget</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1223838393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8754260679566246662">Review courtesy of Dark Faerie Tales<br/><br/>Quick & Dirty: Emotional story that has wonderful romance, interesting characters, and a great life message. This is a great read that I think all young adult fans will enjoy!<br/><br/>Opening Sentence: I am a liar.<br/><br/>The Review:<br/><br/>Sabine is a unique girl that happens to live everyday twice. Every 24 hours at midnight she goes through a shift and she switches between two different lives. In one life she is popular, smart, driven, and comes from a rich family with divorced par</span>
  <span id="freeText8754260679566246662" style="display:none">Review courtesy of Dark Faerie Tales<br /><br />Quick &amp; Dirty: Emotional story that has wonderful romance, interesting characters, and a great life message. This is a great read that I think all young adult fans will enjoy!<br /><br />Opening Sentence: I am a liar.<br /><br />The Review:<br /><br />Sabine is a unique girl that happens to live everyday twice. Every 24 hours at midnight she goes through a shift and she switches between two different lives. In one life she is popular, smart, driven, and comes from a rich family with divorced parents. She also has two older brothers and a super sexy boyfriend. She wears what is in fashion and has a very stable life. In her other life she comes from a poor family where both of her parents work like crazy to make ends meet, but they are still happily married. She has a young sister that she adores and helps take care of since her parents work so much. She has a more gothic style and her group of friends are a little on the rebellious side.<br /><br />As you can see her lives couldn’t be more opposite. The one thing she has noticed is that if she does something physical to herself like dye her hair or break a bone it has always transferred into the other world until recently. She starts to experiment with things to see if she can finally have what she has always wanted, a normal life in only one world. But she soon meets a boy named Ethan that makes her feel things she never thought possible. He makes her realize that maybe her situation isn’t as bad as it seems and just maybe she is lucky to have the opportunity to live two different lives.<br /><br />Sabine is a very diverse character and it was really interesting to see her in the two different worlds. I think the most significant thing about her is that she is so different in both worlds, but really she is not herself in either world because she only lets a certain part of herself show in each world. Watching her struggle with who she really is was hard to watch and made me really connect with her on a deep level. If she ever has any hope of being happy she is going to have to bring both sides of herself into harmony and watching her journey was both inspirational and emotional. I really enjoyed seeing how she handled things differently based on what world she was in, it made her character more interesting to get to know. Her story was very different from anything else I have ever read and I really enjoyed it.<br /><br />Will is Sabine’s boyfriend in her “perfect” world and to be honest I thought he was pretty boring. Sure, he is gorgeous, popular, and supposedly perfect in every way, but I just felt he was a little dry. The chemistry was totally missing between him and Sabine which she openly admits to. I feel like Will’s character was written to be this way and I think that for the most part this was exactly how Shirvington wanted you to feel about his character, so he was actually written perfectly.<br /><br />Ethan is one of those guys that you fall for instantly. He is sweet, sexy, and very understanding. The moments that he spends with Sabine are so adorable and pretty emotional at times. He is one of the only people she has felt she could be totally honest with and not feel like she is being judged. Their relationship develops slowly and it is beautifully done. I loved Ethan and thought that his character was flawless!<br /><br />One Past Midnight is a gut wrenching story that pulls at your heart strings and really makes you think. I felt that the message in this story was very profound and you can learn some important life lessons by reading this book. Every choice we make in life has consequences and the grass isn’t always greener on the other side. But on top of a great message this was an entertaining story that I really enjoyed reading. The characters were interesting, the romance was beautiful, and the plot was intriguing. I did have a little bit of a hard time getting into the story at first because it moved slower then I was expecting but about half way through it got a lot better. This is a standalone novel and while the ending was heart breaking, it was also done perfectly. I am a huge fan of Shirvington’s work and while I didn’t quite like this as much as her Embraced series, I still think that it is worth picking up. I will honestly read anything that Shirvington writes because her stories are just amazing and I look forward to seeing what she comes out with next. Anyone looking for a great story with a wonderful message should pick this one up for sure!<br /><br />Notable Scene:<br /><br />About half an hour before the Shift I changed out of my clothes, shimmying my fitted mini off with one hand and wriggling into my oversized T-shirt nightie. I ditched the sling; it was more hindrance than help. I left my black Doc Martens for last, wincing as I gave a one-handed pull to loosen the laces before using my feet to kick them off.<br /><br />I relied on rituals. Found comfort in the patterns I’d developed over the years. I settled into bed, ignoring the sheen of sweat on my forehead and the sick feeling in my gut as I arranged myself against the pillows as usual, making sure there would be nothing out of the ordinary to return to tomorrow night.<br /><br />I almost made it too.<br /><br />But with only minutes to go, my mouth started its telltale watering. I had to bolt to the bathroom to throw up before hurrying back to bed before midnight struck.<br /><br />The last thoughts that slipped into my mind marked the beginning of the change in my worlds. How could this have happened? How has nothing like this happened to me before?<br /><br />FTC Advisory: Bloomsbury Children’s provided me with a copy of One Past Midnight. No goody bags, sponsorships, “material connections,” or bribes were exchanged for my review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8754260679566246662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2124906141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2124906141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6436065872741414656">I liked the concept and the idea it was the first time that I read a story that have 2 parallèle worlds ..i was intrigued when I read the blurb at first I didn't think that it would be a good story just because I was afraid of the shifting between those 2 completely complex lifes but the writer managed to make it looked effortless and simple.</span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xxa/tXpMC9nyHt8+RATKHXMLVdwjgNZhfSe27TLQGTc4j9IX14eJXFWbHiqfly+IBHfBOAoKmr2/X/91aEdkOg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yD72GI32g3YpDblyMwBGottur1gXD1HySbUlnF4eRVQ3p5u6ID0B846IeGbok6M3rBI7vD6FHS6LzWwEBIk4WQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

With a terrible headache and a major case of déjà vu, she heads home only t<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText4278670672031151030\" style=\"display:none\">A flash of white light . . . and then . . . nothing. \n\nWhen sixteen-year-old Kyra Agnew wakes up behind a Dumpster at the Gas ’n’ Sip, she has no memory of how she got there. With a terrible headache and a major case of déjà vu, she heads home only to discover that five years have passed . . . yet she hasn’t aged a day. \n\nEverything else about Kyra’s old life is different. Her parents are divorced, her boyfriend, Austin, is in college and dating her best friend, and her dad has changed from an uptight neat-freak to a drunken conspiracy theorist who blames her five-year disappearance on little green men. \n\nConfused and lost, Kyra isn’t sure how to move forward unless she uncovers the truth. With Austin gone, she turns to Tyler, Austin’s annoying kid brother, who is now seventeen and who she has a sudden undeniable attraction to. As Tyler and Kyra retrace her steps from the fateful night of her disappearance, they discover strange phenomena that no one can explain, and they begin to wonder if Kyra’s father is not as crazy as he seems. There are others like her who have been taken . . . and returned. Kyra races to find an explanation and reclaim the life she once had, but what if the life she wants back is not her own?<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"4278670672031151030\" href=\"#\"   <span id="freeText3833719188183106034" style="display:none">Jessica Shirvington is the author of THE VIOLET EDEN CHAPTERS also known as THE EMBRACE SERIES, stand alone novel, BETWEEN THE LIVES and has an exciting new duology called DISRUPTION on the way in 2014.<br /> <br />An entrepreneur, author, and mother living in Sydney, Australia, Jessica is also a 2011 &amp; 2012 finalist for Cosmopolitan’s annual Fun, Fearless Female Award. She’s also one of the lucky few who met the love of her life at age seventeen: Matt Shirvington, a former Olympian and current sports broadcaster for Foxtel and Fox Sports. Married for twleve years with two beautiful daughters, Sienna and Winter, Jessica knows her early age romance and its longevity has definitely contributed to how she tackles relationships in her YA novels. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/23683035-between-the-lives">Quotes from Between the Lives</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;You said you wanted someone to know you. Maybe I just want to have someone know me too. Without you in this world, the memories of every moment we’ve shared together will be gone. We only exist because others see us. Part of my existence...an important part, only exists because you are here to see it.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/820052-you-said-you-wanted-someone-to-know-you-maybe-i">51 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;<i>My Sabine,<br />I just left your room. You were so beautiful lying there sound asleep that I couldn’t bear to wake you. But I’m not feeling so great and there are things I promised to tell you that I fear I may not get the chance to.<br />I know you had once hoped that I would be the one to pass on your letters to Maddie once you were gone. But, as it turns out, I think it is going to be me who ends up leaving the letters behind.<br />Be mad at me. You should. But after that try to understand that I did what I thought was best. I wanted to tell you. So many times I snuck down to your room planning on telling you everything, but I just couldn’t.<br />Partly it was for you – yes. You needed time and I didn’t want to influence your choices, even once I realised what was happening between us, even more so then. Falling in love with you only made those choices more complicated and I feared that you might choose to stay for me and then, after I was gone, change your mind. I couldn’t let that happen.<br />Partly the choice was selfish, and for that I am sorry. For so long now people have been trying to fix me, but where they failed, you succeeded. You’ve given me more life in the last couple of weeks that I’ve had in years. Being with you, loving you, making memories with you, fearing for you, wanting to show you the beauty of life instead of the terror – it was bittersweet, but more importantly Sabine, it was real.<br />I know this is the part when I beg you to go on, live your life and be happy. But I don’t need to say those things. I know you. Your lives will be extraordinary. You certainly made mine feel that way.<br />Please find it in your heart to forgive me one day. I wish we had more time, but I want to thank you – for giving me life in my time of death.<br />My love for you is eternal.<br />Ethan.</i>&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/820056-my-sabine-i-just-left-your-room-you-were-so">39 likes</a>
            </nobr>
